Waves and the ocean not only provide a source of movement and randomness, but also align with Portugalâs maritime history and the officeâs scenic view.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, this was easier said than done. It turns out that making a wave machine wall is a real challenge, given that these toys are not as popular as they were in the past,Â  and arenât being manufactured in the size we needed any more. We scoured eBay and other sources but couldn&amp;#39;t find enough, consistent in style and in working order wave machines. We also discovered that off-the-shelf models werenât designed to run 24/7, which was a critical requirement for our use.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Artistry to create wave machines&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;p&gt;Undaunted, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-top-100-most-loved-workplaces-in-2022\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflareâs Places team&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which ensures our offices reflect our values and culture, found a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://wavemotionmachines.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;U.S.-based artisan&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that specializes in ocean wave displays to create the wave machines for us. Since 2009, his one-person business, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://wavemotionmachines.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Hughes Wave Motion Machines&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, has blended artistry, engineering, and research, following his transition from Lockheed Martin Space Systems, where he designed military and commercial satellites.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div style=\&quot;position: relative; padding-top: 56.25%;\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;iframe\n    src=\&quot;https://customer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com/82638d9e81c68911d07fc2a0db093b74/iframe?muted=true&amp;preload=true&amp;poster=https%3A%2F%2Fcustomer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com%2F82638d9e81c68911d07fc2a0db093b74%2Fthumbnails%2Fthumbnail.jpg%3Ftime%3D%26height%3D600\&quot;\n    loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;\n    style=\&quot;border: none; position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; height: 100%; width: 100%;\&quot;\n    allow=\&quot;accelerometer; gyroscope; autoplay; encrypted-media; picture-in-picture;\&quot;\n    allowfullscreen=\&quot;true\&quot;\n  &gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Timelapse of the mesmerizing office waves, set to the tune of an AI-generated song.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Collaborating closely, we developed a custom rectangular wave machine (18 inches/45 cm long) that runs nonstop â not an easy task â which required hundreds of hours of testing and many iterations. Featuring rotating wheels, continuous motors, and a unique fluid formula, these machines create realistic ocean-like waves in green, blue, and Cloudflareâs signature orange.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Hereâs a quote from the artist himself about these wave machines:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;âThe machineâs design is a balancing act of matching components and their placement to how the fluid responds in a given configuration. There is a complex yet delicate relationship between viscosity, specific gravity, the size and design of the vessel, and the placement of each mechanical interface. Everything must be precisely aligned, centered around the fluid like a mathematical function. I like to say itâs akin to âbalancing a checkerboard on a beach ball in the wind.ââ&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3K9fpTU0D0xi831MHFOFBj/570b8c307fea1078f3c0262e13447bf6/image7.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1500\&quot; height=\&quot;1999\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;The Cloudflare Places Team with Lisbon office architects and contractor testing wave machine placement, shelves, lighting, and mirrors to enhance movement and reflection, March 2024.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Despite delays, the Lisbon wave machines finally debuted on March 10, 2025 â an incredibly exciting moment for the Places team.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Some numbers about our wave-machine entropy wall:&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;50 wave machines, 50 motion wheels &amp;amp; motors, 50 acrylic containers filled with Hughes Wave Fluid Formula (two &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.sciencedirect.com/topics/engineering/immiscible-liquid\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;immiscible liquids&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;3 liquid colors: blue, green, and orange&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;15 months from concept to completion&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;14 flips (side-to-side balancing movements) per minute â over 20,000 per day&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over 15 waves per minute&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;~0.5 liters of liquid per machine&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;lavarand-origins-and-walls-of-entropy\&quot;&gt;LavaRand origins and walls of entropy&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#lavarand-origins-and-walls-of-entropy\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Cloudflareâs servers handle 71 million HTTP requests per second on average, with 100 million HTTP requests per second at peak. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/adoption-and-usage#http-vs-https\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Most of these requests are secured via TLS&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which relies on secure randomness for cryptographic integrity. A Cryptographically Secure Pseudorandom Number Generator (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ssl/lava-lamp-encryption/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CSPRNG&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) ensures unpredictability, but only when seeded with high-quality entropy. Since chaotic movement in the real world is truly random, Cloudflare designed a system to harness it. Our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/harnessing-office-chaos/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;2024 blog post&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; expands on this topic in a more technical way, but hereâs a quick summary.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/randomness-101-lavarand-in-production/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;2017&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, Cloudflare launched LavaRand, inspired by &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.wired.com/1997/03/lava-lites-easy-to-break-hard-to-crack/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Silicon Graphicsâ 1997 concept&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; However, the need for randomness in security was already a hot topic on our blog before that, such as in our discussions of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/why-randomness-matters/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;securing systems&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/a-relatively-easy-to-understand-primer-on-elliptic-curve-cryptography/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;cryptography&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Originally, LavaRand collected entropy from a wall of lava lamps in our San Francisco office, feeding an internal API that servers periodically query to include in their entropy pools. Over time, we expanded LavaRand beyond lava lamps, incorporating &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/harnessing-office-chaos/#londons-unpredictable-pendulums\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;new sources of office chaos&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; while maintaining the same core method.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2v6Wvde8j8R7482QjBsSrV/89b37c652654e27c13d328e9acac6489/image9.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1612\&quot; height=\&quot;381\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;A camera captures images of dynamic, unpredictable randomness displays. Shadows, lighting changes, and even sensor noise contribute entropy. Each image is then processed into a compact hash, converting it into a sequence of random bytes. These, combined with the previous seed and local system entropy, serve as input for a Key Derivation Function (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Key_derivation_function\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;KDF&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), which generates a new seed for a CSPRNG â capable of producing virtually unlimited random bytes upon request. The waves in our Lisbon office are now contributing to this pool of randomness.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1XFFjr4jhRMQlz6akHKZm4/44759c4e879de3792cd21b4ce2525c90/image5.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1491\&quot; height=\&quot;400\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflareâs LavaRand API makes this randomness accessible internally, strengthening cryptographic security across our global infrastructure. For example, when you use &lt;i&gt;Math.random()&lt;/i&gt; in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://workers.cloudflare.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Workers&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, part of that randomness comes from LavaRand. Similarly, querying our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/harnessing-office-chaos/#drand-distributed-and-verifiable-public-randomness\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;drand API&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; taps into LavaRand as well. Cloudflare offers this API to enable anyone to generate random numbers and even seed their own systems.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;our-new-lisbon-office-space\&quot;&gt;Our new Lisbon office space&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#our-new-lisbon-office-space\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        \n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5ivPkCfTkGxfo6Swt6p9qY/e7414a14b88bef7ac7e0ef6f737b58c6/image8.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1330\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Photo of the view from our Lisbon office, featuring ceiling lights arranged in a wave-like pattern.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Entropy also inspired the design ethos of our new Lisbon office, given that the wall of waves and the office are part of the same project. As soon as you enter, you&amp;#39;re greeted not only by the motion of the entropy wall but also by the constant movement of planet Earth on our Cloudflare Radar Display screen that stands next to it. But the waves donât stop there â more elements throughout the space mimic the dynamic flow of the Internet itself. Unlike ocean tides, however, Internet traffic ebbs and flows with the motion of the Sun, not the Moon.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;As you walk through the office, waves are everywhere â in the ceiling lights, the architectural contours, and even the floor plan, thoughtfully designed by our architect to reflect the fluid movement of water. The visual elements create a cohesive experience, reinforcing a sense of motion. Each meeting room embraces this maritime theme, named after famous Portuguese beaches â including, naturally, NazarÃ©.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We partnered with an incredible group of local Portuguese vendors for this construction project, where all the leads were women â something incredibly rare for the industry. The local teams worked with passion, proudly wore Cloudflare t-shirts, and fostered a warm, family-like atmosphere. They openly expressed pride in the project, sharing how it stood out from anything they had worked on before.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7lpuurEtWfpIPKvHVqmD0L/0b0561097859f286d6b5e98db82f1e0f/image3.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1125\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Our amazing third-party team and internal Places team, proudly rocking Cloudflare shirts after bringing this project to life.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;help-us-select-a-name-for-our-new-wall-of-entropy\&quot;&gt;Help us select a name for our new wall of entropy&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#help-us-select-a-name-for-our-new-wall-of-entropy\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Next, we have several name options for this new wall of entropy. recently, this new wall of entropy began with an idea back in 2023: âWhat could we use for randomness that was like our lava lamp wall in San Francisco but represented our team in Portugal?â&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The original inspiration came from wave motion machine desk toys, which were popular among some of our team members. Waves and the ocean not only provide a source of movement and randomness, but also align with Portugalâs maritime history and the officeâs scenic view.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, this was easier said than done. It turns out that making a wave machine wall is a real challenge, given that these toys are not as popular as they were in the past,Â  and arenât being manufactured in the size we needed any more. We scoured eBay and other sources but couldn&amp;#39;t find enough, consistent in style and in working order wave machines. We also discovered that off-the-shelf models werenât designed to run 24/7, which was a critical requirement for our use.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Artistry to create wave machines&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;p&gt;Undaunted, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-top-100-most-loved-workplaces-in-2022\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflareâs Places team&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which ensures our offices reflect our values and culture, found a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://wavemotionmachines.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;U.S.-based artisan&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that specializes in ocean wave displays to create the wave machines for us. Since 2009, his one-person business, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://wavemotionmachines.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Hughes Wave Motion Machines&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, has blended artistry, engineering, and research, following his transition from Lockheed Martin Space Systems, where he designed military and commercial satellites.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div style=\&quot;position: relative; padding-top: 56.25%;\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;iframe\n    src=\&quot;https://customer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com/82638d9e81c68911d07fc2a0db093b74/iframe?muted=true&amp;preload=true&amp;poster=https%3A%2F%2Fcustomer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com%2F82638d9e81c68911d07fc2a0db093b74%2Fthumbnails%2Fthumbnail.jpg%3Ftime%3D%26height%3D600\&quot;\n    loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;\n    style=\&quot;border: none; position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; height: 100%; width: 100%;\&quot;\n    allow=\&quot;accelerometer; gyroscope; autoplay; encrypted-media; picture-in-picture;\&quot;\n    allowfullscreen=\&quot;true\&quot;\n  &gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Timelapse of the mesmerizing office waves, set to the tune of an AI-generated song.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Collaborating closely, we developed a custom rectangular wave machine (18 inches/45 cm long) that runs nonstop â not an easy task â which required hundreds of hours of testing and many iterations. Featuring rotating wheels, continuous motors, and a unique fluid formula, these machines create realistic ocean-like waves in green, blue, and Cloudflareâs signature orange.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Hereâs a quote from the artist himself about these wave machines:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;âThe machineâs design is a balancing act of matching components and their placement to how the fluid responds in a given configuration. There is a complex yet delicate relationship between viscosity, specific gravity, the size and design of the vessel, and the placement of each mechanical interface. Everything must be precisely aligned, centered around the fluid like a mathematical function. I like to say itâs akin to âbalancing a checkerboard on a beach ball in the wind.ââ&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3K9fpTU0D0xi831MHFOFBj/570b8c307fea1078f3c0262e13447bf6/image7.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1500\&quot; height=\&quot;1999\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;The Cloudflare Places Team with Lisbon office architects and contractor testing wave machine placement, shelves, lighting, and mirrors to enhance movement and reflection, March 2024.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Despite delays, the Lisbon wave machines finally debuted on March 10, 2025 â an incredibly exciting moment for the Places team.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Some numbers about our wave-machine entropy wall:&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;50 wave machines, 50 motion wheels &amp;amp; motors, 50 acrylic containers filled with Hughes Wave Fluid Formula (two &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.sciencedirect.com/topics/engineering/immiscible-liquid\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;immiscible liquids&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;3 liquid colors: blue, green, and orange&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;15 months from concept to completion&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;14 flips (side-to-side balancing movements) per minute â over 20,000 per day&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over 15 waves per minute&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;~0.5 liters of liquid per machine&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;lavarand-origins-and-walls-of-entropy\&quot;&gt;LavaRand origins and walls of entropy&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#lavarand-origins-and-walls-of-entropy\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Cloudflareâs servers handle 71 million HTTP requests per second on average, with 100 million HTTP requests per second at peak. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/adoption-and-usage#http-vs-https\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Most of these requests are secured via TLS&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which relies on secure randomness for cryptographic integrity. A Cryptographically Secure Pseudorandom Number Generator (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ssl/lava-lamp-encryption/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CSPRNG&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) ensures unpredictability, but only when seeded with high-quality entropy. Since chaotic movement in the real world is truly random, Cloudflare designed a system to harness it. Our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/harnessing-office-chaos/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;2024 blog post&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; expands on this topic in a more technical way, but hereâs a quick summary.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/randomness-101-lavarand-in-production/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;2017&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, Cloudflare launched LavaRand, inspired by &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.wired.com/1997/03/lava-lites-easy-to-break-hard-to-crack/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Silicon Graphicsâ 1997 concept&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; However, the need for randomness in security was already a hot topic on our blog before that, such as in our discussions of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/why-randomness-matters/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;securing systems&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/a-relatively-easy-to-understand-primer-on-elliptic-curve-cryptography/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;cryptography&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Originally, LavaRand collected entropy from a wall of lava lamps in our San Francisco office, feeding an internal API that servers periodically query to include in their entropy pools. Over time, we expanded LavaRand beyond lava lamps, incorporating &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/harnessing-office-chaos/#londons-unpredictable-pendulums\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;new sources of office chaos&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; while maintaining the same core method.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2v6Wvde8j8R7482QjBsSrV/89b37c652654e27c13d328e9acac6489/image9.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1612\&quot; height=\&quot;381\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;A camera captures images of dynamic, unpredictable randomness displays. Shadows, lighting changes, and even sensor noise contribute entropy. Each image is then processed into a compact hash, converting it into a sequence of random bytes. These, combined with the previous seed and local system entropy, serve as input for a Key Derivation Function (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Key_derivation_function\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;KDF&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), which generates a new seed for a CSPRNG â capable of producing virtually unlimited random bytes upon request. The waves in our Lisbon office are now contributing to this pool of randomness.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1XFFjr4jhRMQlz6akHKZm4/44759c4e879de3792cd21b4ce2525c90/image5.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1491\&quot; height=\&quot;400\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflareâs LavaRand API makes this randomness accessible internally, strengthening cryptographic security across our global infrastructure. For example, when you use &lt;i&gt;Math.random()&lt;/i&gt; in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://workers.cloudflare.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Workers&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, part of that randomness comes from LavaRand. Similarly, querying our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/harnessing-office-chaos/#drand-distributed-and-verifiable-public-randomness\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;drand API&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; taps into LavaRand as well. Cloudflare offers this API to enable anyone to generate random numbers and even seed their own systems.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;our-new-lisbon-office-space\&quot;&gt;Our new Lisbon office space&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#our-new-lisbon-office-space\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        \n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5ivPkCfTkGxfo6Swt6p9qY/e7414a14b88bef7ac7e0ef6f737b58c6/image8.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1330\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Photo of the view from our Lisbon office, featuring ceiling lights arranged in a wave-like pattern.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Entropy also inspired the design ethos of our new Lisbon office, given that the wall of waves and the office are part of the same project. As soon as you enter, you&amp;#39;re greeted not only by the motion of the entropy wall but also by the constant movement of planet Earth on our Cloudflare Radar Display screen that stands next to it. But the waves donât stop there â more elements throughout the space mimic the dynamic flow of the Internet itself. Unlike ocean tides, however, Internet traffic ebbs and flows with the motion of the Sun, not the Moon.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;As you walk through the office, waves are everywhere â in the ceiling lights, the architectural contours, and even the floor plan, thoughtfully designed by our architect to reflect the fluid movement of water. The visual elements create a cohesive experience, reinforcing a sense of motion. Each meeting room embraces this maritime theme, named after famous Portuguese beaches â including, naturally, NazarÃ©.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We partnered with an incredible group of local Portuguese vendors for this construction project, where all the leads were women â something incredibly rare for the industry. The local teams worked with passion, proudly wore Cloudflare t-shirts, and fostered a warm, family-like atmosphere. They openly expressed pride in the project, sharing how it stood out from anything they had worked on before.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7lpuurEtWfpIPKvHVqmD0L/0b0561097859f286d6b5e98db82f1e0f/image3.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1125\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Our amazing third-party team and internal Places team, proudly rocking Cloudflare shirts after bringing this project to life.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;help-us-select-a-name-for-our-new-wall-of-entropy\&quot;&gt;Help us select a name for our new wall of entropy&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#help-us-select-a-name-for-our-new-wall-of-entropy\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Next, we have several name options for this new wall of entropy. announce support for Zero Trust datasets, and custom dashboards where customers can monitor critical metrics for suspicious or unusual activity. &quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;In 2024, we &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;announced Log Explorer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, giving customers the ability to store and query their HTTP and security event logs natively within the Cloudflare network. Today, we are excited to announce that Log Explorer now supports logs from our Zero Trust product suite. In addition, customers can create custom dashboards to monitor suspicious or unusual activity.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Every day, Cloudflare detects and protects customers against billions of threats, including DDoS attacks, bots, web application exploits, and more. SOC analysts, who are charged with keeping their companies safe from the growing spectre of Internet threats, may want to investigate these threats to gain additional insights on attacker behavior and protect against future attacks. Log Explorer, by collecting logs from various Cloudflare products, provides a single starting point for investigations. As a result, analysts can avoid forwarding logs to other tools, maximizing productivity and minimizing costs. Further, analysts can monitor signals specific to their organizations using custom dashboards.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;zero-trust-dataset-support-in-log-explorer\&quot;&gt;Zero Trust dataset support in Log Explorer&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#zero-trust-dataset-support-in-log-explorer\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;Log Explorer stores your Cloudflare logs for a 30-day retention period so that you can analyze them natively and in a single interface, within the Cloudflare Dashboard. Cloudflare log data is diverse, reflecting the breadth of capabilities available.Â  For example, HTTP requests contain information about the client such as their IP address, request method, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/network-layer/what-is-an-autonomous-system/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;autonomous system (ASN)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, request paths, and TLS versions used. Additionally, Cloudflareâs Application Security &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;WAF Detections&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; enrich these HTTP request logs with additional context, such as the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/attack-score/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;WAF attack score&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, to identify threats.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today we are announcing that seven additional Cloudflare product datasets are now available in Log Explorer. These seven datasets are the logs generated from our Zero Trust product suite, and include logs from &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/access_requests/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Access&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/gateway_dns/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Gateway DNS&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/gateway_http/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Gateway HTTP&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/gateway_network/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Gateway Network&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/casb_findings/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CASB&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/zero_trust_network_sessions/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;ZeroÂ &lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/zero_trust_network_sessions/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Trust Network Session&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/account/device_posture_results/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Device Posture Results&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Read on for examples of how to use these logs to identify common threats.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;investigating-unauthorized-access\&quot;&gt;Investigating unauthorized access&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#investigating-unauthorized-access\&quot; For instance, companies in the retail or financial industries worry about fraud, while every company is concerned about data exfiltration, of information like trade secrets. And any form of personally identifiable information (PII) is a target for data breaches or ransomware attacks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While log exploration helps you react to threats, our new custom dashboards allow you to define the specific metrics you need in order to monitor threats you are concerned about.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Getting started is easy, with the ability to create a chart using natural language. A natural language interface is integrated into the chart create/edit experience, enabling you to describe in your own words the chart you want to create. Similar to the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/security-analytics-ai-assistant/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;AI Assistant&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; we announced during Security Week 2024, the prompt translates your language to the appropriate chart configuration, which can then be added to a new or existing custom dashboard.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Use a prompt&lt;/b&gt;: Enter a query like âCompare status code ranges over timeâ. The AI model decides the most appropriate visualization and constructs your chart configuration.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Customize your chart&lt;/b&gt;: Select the chart elements manually, including the chart type, title, dataset to query, metrics, and filters. To that end, during 2023âs Security Week, we &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/radar-url-scanner-early-access/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;launched our URL Scanner&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which enables users to safely scan any URL to determine if it is safe to view or interact with. During 2024âs Security Week, we &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/email-security-insights-on-cloudflare-radar/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;launched an Email Security page&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which provides a unique perspective on the threats posed by malicious emails, spam volume, the adoption of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/email-security/dmarc-dkim-spf/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;email authentication methods like SPF, DMARC, and DKIM&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and the use of IPv4/IPv6 and TLS by email servers. For Security Week 2025, we are adding several new DDoS-focused graphs, new insights into leaked credential trends, and a new &lt;b&gt;Bots&lt;/b&gt; page to Cloudflare Radar.Â  We are also taking this opportunity to refactor Radarâs &lt;b&gt;Security &amp;amp; Attacks&lt;/b&gt; page, breaking it out into &lt;b&gt;Application Layer&lt;/b&gt; and &lt;b&gt;Network Layer&lt;/b&gt; sections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Below, we review all of these changes and additions to Radar.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;layered-security\&quot;&gt;Layered security&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#layered-security\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Since Cloudflare Radar launched in 2020, it has included both network layer (Layers 3 &amp;amp; 4) and application layer (Layer 7) attack traffic insights on a single &lt;b&gt;Security &amp;amp; Attacks&lt;/b&gt; page. Over the last four-plus years, we have evolved some of the existing data sets on the page, as well as adding new ones. As the page has grown and improved over time, it risked becoming unwieldy to navigate, making it hard to find the graphs and data of interest. To help address that, the &lt;b&gt;Security&lt;/b&gt; section on Radar now features separate &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Application Layer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/network-layer\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Network Layer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt; pages. The &lt;b&gt;Application Layer&lt;/b&gt; page is the default, and includes insights from analysis of HTTP-based malicious and attack traffic. The &lt;b&gt;Network Layer&lt;/b&gt; page includes insights from analysis of network and transport layer attacks, as well as observed &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/tcp-resets-timeouts/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;TCP resets and timeouts&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Future security and attack-related data sets will be added to the relevant page. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/email-security\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Email Security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt; remains on its own dedicated page.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3zxFA8iG7N9MZQzAQAaCNf/ee92891b74b0d70052cc43239dad656f/image__2_.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2400\&quot; height=\&quot;704\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;a-geographic-and-network-view-of-application-layer-ddos-attacks\&quot;&gt;A geographic and network view of application layer DDoS attacks&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#a-geographic-and-network-view-of-application-layer-ddos-attacks\&quot; have historically provided insights, aggregated on a quarterly basis, into the top source and target locations of application layer DDoS attacks. A &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer#application-layer-ddos-attacks-distribution\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;new map and table&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; on Radarâs &lt;b&gt;Application Layer&lt;/b&gt; Security page now provide more timely insights, with a global choropleth map showing a geographical distribution of source and target locations, and an accompanying list of the top 20 locations by share of all DDoS requests. Source location attribution continues to rely on the geolocation of the IP address originating the blocked request, while target location remains the billing location of the account that owns the site being attacked.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over the first week of March 2025, the United States, Indonesia, and Germany were the top sources of application layer DDoS attacks, together accounting for over 30% of such attacks as shown below. The concentration across the top targeted locations was quite different, with customers from Canada, the United States, and Singapore attracting 56% of application layer DDoS attacks.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7nW8CyC5L4s68ntQEe1pfT/a8b571b9b2325f5f71936367e8879af1/image10.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;1216\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;In addition to extended visibility into the geographic source of application layer DDoS attacks, we have also added &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/network-layer/what-is-an-autonomous-system/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;autonomous system (AS)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;-level visibility. A &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer#application-layer-ddos-attacks-source-as-distribution\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;new treemap&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; view shows the distribution of these attacks by source AS. At a global level, the largest sources include cloud/hosting providers in Germany, the United States, China, and Vietnam.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/332A6OGGKUNCE0wLVBKBmd/2b93c6bd46105602214d7ced2ead71b6/image7.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;1020\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;For a selected country/region, the treemap displays a source AS distribution for attacks observed to be originating from that location. In some, the sources of attack traffic are heavily concentrated in consumer/business network providers, such as in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer/pt#application-layer-ddos-attacks-source-as-distribution\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Portugal&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, shown below. However, in other countries/regions that have a large cloud provider presence, such as &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer/ie#application-layer-ddos-attacks-source-as-distribution\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Ireland&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer/sg#application-layer-ddos-attacks-source-as-distribution\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Singapore&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer/us#application-layer-ddos-attacks-source-as-distribution\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;United States&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, ASNs associated with these types of providers are the dominant sources. To that end, Singapore was listed as being among the top sources of application layer DDoS attacks in each of the quarterly DDoS threat reports in 2024.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3RpwYjFjmTR2WFx5UpsUuS/5211c6e5afd4733185ba1ed03750d1d2/image3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;1020\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;have-you-been-pwned\&quot;&gt;Have you been pwned?&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#have-you-been-pwned\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Every week, it seems like thereâs another headline about a data breach, talking about thousands or millions of usernames and passwords being stolen. Or maybe you get an email from an identity monitoring service that your username and password were found on the âdark webâ. (Of course, youâre getting those alerts thanks to a complementary subscription to the service offered as penance from another data breachâ¦)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This credential theft is especially problematic because people often reuse passwords, despite best practices advising the use of strong, unique passwords for each site or application. To help mitigate this risk, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/a-safer-internet-with-cloudflare/#account-takeover-detection\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;starting in 2024&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, Cloudflare began enabling customers to scan authentication requests for their websites and applications using a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/privacy-preserving-compromised-credential-checking/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;privacy-preserving&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; compromised credential checker implementation to detect known-leaked usernames and passwords. Today, we&amp;#39;re using aggregated data to display trends in how often these leaked and stolen credentials are observed across Cloudflare&amp;#39;s network. (Here, we are defining âleaked credentialsâ as usernames or passwords being found in a public dataset, or the username and password detected as being similar.)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/leaked-credentials/#how-it-works\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Leaked credentials detection&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; scans incoming HTTP requests for known authentication patterns from common web apps and any custom detection locations that were configured. The service uses a privacy-preserving compromised credential checking protocol to compare a hash of the detected passwords to hashes of compromised passwords found in databases of leaked credentials. A &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer#leaked-credentials-usage\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;new Radar graph&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; on the worldwide &lt;b&gt;Application Layer&lt;/b&gt; Security page provides visibility into aggregate trends around the detection of leaked credentials in authentication requests. Filterable by authentication requests from human users, bots, or all (human + bot), the graph shows the distribution requests classified as âcleanâ (no leaked credentials detected) and âcompromisedâ (leaked credentials, as defined above, were used). At a worldwide level, we found that for the first week of March 2025, leaked credentials were used in 64% of all, over 65% of bot, and over 44% of human authorization requests. &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5r8sHbOTrQ1ceGpLa0d3Dn/4ea9ab5b342cd394bd096349d4907ab0/image6.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;762\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;This suggests that from a human perspective, password reuse is still a problem, as is users not taking immediate actions to change passwords when notified of a breach. And from a bot perspective, this suggests that attackers know that there is a good chance that leaked credentials for one website or application will enable them to access that same userâs account elsewhere.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;As a complement to the leaked credentials data, Radar is also now providing a worldwide view into the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/application-layer#bot-vs-human\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;share of authentication requests originating from bots&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Note that not all of these requests are necessarily malicious â while some may be associated with credential stuffing-style attacks, others may be from automated scripts or other benign applications accessing an authentication endpoint. (Having said that, automated malicious attack request volume far exceeds legitimate automated login attempts.) During the first week of March 2025, we found that over 94% of authentication requests came from bots (were automated), with the balance coming from humans. Over that same period, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/traffic?dateStart=2025-03-01&amp;dateEnd=2025-03-07#bot-vs-human\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;bot traffic only accounted for 30% of overall requests&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. So although bots donât represent a majority of request traffic, authentication requests appear to comprise a significant portion of their activity.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/20tYE9sH7SOnJDsnh28ZYz/3c33320a0a7406a348c4b92d22f469ed/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;762\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;bots-get-a-dedicated-page\&quot;&gt;Bots get a dedicated page&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#bots-get-a-dedicated-page\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;As a reminder, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/en-gb/learning/bots/what-is-a-bot/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;bot&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; traffic describes any non-human Internet traffic, and monitoring bot levels can help spot potential malicious activities. Of course, bots can be helpful too, and Cloudflare maintains a list of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/bots#verified-bots\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;verified bots&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to help keep the Internet healthy. Given the importance of monitoring bot activity, we have launched a new dedicated &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/bots\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Bots&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt; page in the Traffic section of Cloudflare Radar to support these efforts. For both worldwide and location views over the selected time period, the page shows the distribution of bot (automated) vs. human HTTP requests, as well as a graph showing bot traffic trends. (Our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/bots/concepts/bot-score/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;bot score&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, combining machine learning, heuristics, and other techniques, is used to identify automated requests likely to be coming from bots.)Â &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5bvoSNcGRbc2I5RGhZoIdo/948eca1e82148a1db6130295c0ea2f42/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;690\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Both the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/year-in-review/2023/#bot-traffic-sources\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;2023&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/year-in-review/2024#bot-traffic-sources\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;2024&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; Cloudflare Radar Year in Review microsites included a âBot Traffic Sourcesâ section, showing the locations and networks that Cloudflare determined that the largest shares of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/bots/concepts/bot-score/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;automated/likely automated&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; traffic was originating from. However, these traffic shares were published just once a year, aggregating traffic from January through the end of November.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In order to provide a more timely perspective, these insights are now available on the new Radar Bots page. Similar to the new DDoS attacks content discussed above, the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/bots#bot-traffic-sources\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;worldwide view&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; includes a choropleth map and table illustrating the locations originating the largest shares of all bot traffic. (Note that a similar &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/traffic#traffic-characteristics\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Traffic Characteristics&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; map and table on the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/traffic\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Traffic Overview page&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; ranks locations by the bot traffic share of the locationâs total traffic.) Similar to Year in Review data linked above, the United States continues to originate the largest share of bot traffic.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/RPCiFgeihzYIbm4XIdQ1r/ae9afa59586266c785e4e9dfa8cb3428/image11.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;1214\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;In addition, the worldwide view also breaks out &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/bots#bot-traffic-share-by-autonomous-system\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;bot traffic share by AS&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, mirroring the treemap shown in the Year in Review. As we have noted &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/radar-2024-year-in-review/#the-united-states-was-responsible-for-over-a-third-of-global-bot-traffic-amazon-web-services-was-responsible-for-12-7-of-global-bot-traffic-and-7-8-came-from-google\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;previously&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, cloud platform providers account for a significant amount of bot traffic.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5CsXZNKOZ2ssiVaUzVVM51/5d8ad8b6a257eb0413be19fa101806c9/image8.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;1018\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;At a location level, depending on the country/region selected, the top sources of bot traffic may be cloud/hosting providers, consumer/business network providers, or a mix. For instance, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/bots/fr#bot-traffic-sources\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Franceâs distribution&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is shown below, and four ASNs account for just over half of the countryâs bot traffic. Of these ASNs, two (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/as16276\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;AS16276&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/as12876\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;AS12876&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) belong to cloud/hosting providers, and two (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/as3215\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;AS3215&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/as12322\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;AS12322&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) belong to network providers.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/4RM9zvPRa8NzfdTOFMvMcB/b04d53dd725d1890918668775b551004/image9.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1834\&quot; height=\&quot;1018\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;In addition, the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/bots#verified-bots\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Verified Bots list&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; has been moved to the new Bots page on Radar. The data shown and functionality remains unchanged, and links to the old location will automatically be redirected to the new one.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;summary\&quot;&gt;Summary&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#summary\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;The Cloudflare dashboard provides customers with specific views of security trends, application and network layer attacks, and bot activity across their sites and applications. While these views are useful at an individual customer level, aggregated views at a worldwide, location, and network level provide a macro-level perspective on trends and activity. These aggregated views available on Cloudflare Radar not only help customers understand how their observations compare to the larger whole, but they also help the industry understand emerging threats that may require action.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The underlying data for the graphs and data discussed above is available via the Radar API (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api/resources/radar/subresources/attacks/subresources/layer7/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Application Layer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api/resources/radar/subresources/attacks/subresources/layer3/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Network Layer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api/resources/radar/subresources/http/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Bots&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/api/resources/radar/subresources/leaked_credential_checks/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Leaked Credentials&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;). The data can also be interactively explored in more detail across locations, networks, and time periods using Radarâs &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/explorer\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Data Explorer and AI Assistant&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Maintaining a healthy security posture entails monitoring and strengthening your security defenses to identify risks, ensure compliance, and protect against evolving threats. With our newest capabilities, you can now use Cloudflare to achieve a healthy posture across your SaaS and web applications. This addresses any security teamâs ultimate (daily) question: &lt;i&gt;How well are our assets and documents protected&lt;/i&gt;?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A predictive security posture relies on the following key components:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Real-time discovery and inventory of all your assets and documents&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Continuous asset-aware threat detection and risk assessment&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Prioritised remediation suggestions to increase your protection&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, we are sharing how we have built these key components across SaaS and web applications, and how you can use them to manage your businessâs security posture.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;your-security-posture-at-a-glance\&quot;&gt;Your security posture at a glance&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#your-security-posture-at-a-glance\&quot;
